The second perspective of a smart contract is in execution mode. I recommend to make a new symbol that represents these two dimensions. The consortium is just what we call a particular group of organizations. It's not structural so much as it's definitional (if that was actually a word). The policies are defined by the members/organizations. And those policies are even themselves not particularly structural, it seems to me. Regardless of the specific policies that are defined, the network structure isn't going to change (within reason). It's still going to have peers, channels, an ordering service, smart contracts, ledgers, and so on. 

Could be that I'm just seeing the scope of this doc somewhat differently than you guys. My sense is that we're talking (or should be talking) here about what the structure of a network *is*, rather than *how* and *where* that structure is defined.</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Chris Gabriel - alaskadd@gmail.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L26](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/52bc4c49de8e4a72e22fb3c521cdfcb7e1938531/docs/source/network/network.md#L26)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>Done</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Anthony O'Dowd - a_o-dowd@uk.ibm.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L30](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/52bc4c49de8e4a72e22fb3c521cdfcb7e1938531/docs/source/network/network.md#L30)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>x Make clear CA network relationship

The idea is that CAs create "identities" through a PKI, while MSPs define which identities will have roles (permissions) at every level of the network (channel and local). CAs get you in the door, in other words, while MSPs define what you can do once you're in there. I do like the order you have here, though. A trusted CA must issue a cert first, then MSPs define the permissions the owner of the cert has.

I realize this is all newly written up, but it seems to me that linking out to other docs is going to be critical in this one.</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Chris Gabriel - alaskadd@gmail.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L32](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/52bc4c49de8e4a72e22fb3c521cdfcb7e1938531/docs/source/network/network.md#L32)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>Done</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Joe Alewine - Joe.Alewine@ibm.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L44](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/52bc4c49de8e4a72e22fb3c521cdfcb7e1938531/docs/source/network/network.md#L44)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>This is actually too much of a simplification, imo. Better to say, first, that peers are joined to channels by the organizations that own them. And then that all of the peers on a channel maintain an identical copy of the ledger for that channel. 

Yes, we haven't introduced the concept of a peer yet, but I'd actually argue that you have to understand a peer before you understand a channel (conceptually it's possible to imagine a network without a channel -- or with a single channel that makes the abstraction layer of a channel unnecessary to understand).

They're subnets, or overlays. We have never really been able to nail it down. I think Anthony is right to talk about channels in the context of communication. That's what they actually are, in any case, private messaging paths through the ordering service.

The business requirements for the blockchain network example

The organizations RA, RB, RC and RD have decided to jointly invest in a Hyperledger Fabric blockchain network. Organization RA will contribute 3 peers, and 2 client applications of RA will consume the services of the blockchain network. Organization RB will contribute 4 peers, and has 1 client application. Organization RC contributes 3 peers, and has 2 client applications. Organization RD contributes 4 orderers. 
Organization RA and RB have decided to form a consortium, and exploit a separate application channel between the two of them. Organization RB and RC have decided to form another consortium and also exploit a separate application channel between the two of them. Each application channel has its own channel policy. 
The orderer has associated with it a network policy. 
Company RA has paid substantial fees to more than one consultancy organization to get solid advice how to produce a binding contract now wrt to the modifications that RA considered needed as soon as the relevant software is officially released. In the legally binding agreement signed between RA, RB, RC and RD, the following two clauses appear: the RA-RB channel will use the CFT ordering service as soon as it is officially released as production grade software; the RB-RB channel will use the etcd-RAFT service as soon as it is officially released as production grade software. The power (in the legal meaning of Hohfeld) to realize this transition is only up to organization RA.</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Chris Gabriel - alaskadd@gmail.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L12](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/73a92b7583f758f33151f425d7692e4a02db42cd/docs/source/network/network.md#L12)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>Done</pre><strong>Commenter</strong>: Nikhil Gupta - negupta@us.ibm.com<br><strong>CommentLine</strong>: [docs/source/network/network.md#L22](https://github.com/hyperledger-gerrit-archive/fabric/blob/73a92b7583f758f33151f425d7692e4a02db42cd/docs/source/network/network.md#L22)<br><strong>Comment</strong>: <pre>I would put a section of policies that channels and the network have to maintain in as plain English as possible, ie who can participate, who has to sign off on a new transaction and chaincode, who has to approve an update, so that when we talk about forming the network or a channel, we have the context of what policies are included in that decision. It does cost little time now and it might cost much more in the future.
1. The little circle with contents 1 attached to the left part of CP1 has a different meaning from the little circles with contents 1 at the low side of client app A1, or at the low side of peer P1 and P2 as well as O. The meaning of the circle with contents 1 attached to CP1 means: channel Policy 1 is associated with channel C1. The meaning of all other circles with contents 1 is: this node can make use of the communication facilities of channel C1.
